This is a copy of the text contained in the source code with added.
The complete ouput of the result has been added to the end of this text
together with the entire output of the brute force check.

The pdf contained in this folder further illustrates how the algorithm works
and how the generated graphs look like.


@author Olaf Christ
@email Christ_p@gmx.de


This code generates gene sequences with a Hamming distance of at least 3
between each other. A brute force approach using list operations quickly
becomes infeasible for long sequences due to the very large amount of
comparisons, thus this particular implementation uses a graph theoretic
approach instead. This implementation does not need any third party libraries
such as graph libraries. The simplest way to compile and run the code is to
open the Netbeans project.
How it works:

Step 1: Given a desired sequence length, a complete undirected graph of all
possible sequences is generated first.

Note, that by construction, all child nodes of some node have been generated
by applying a single point mutation per symbol and per node. E.g the child
nodes of node "AA" are CA, GA, TA, AC, AG and AT and are generated by
mutation a single base of the parent node AA. To get sequences with a Hamming
distance of 2 w.r.t AA, we need to further mutate the child nodes of AA and
get CC, CG, CT, GT, TC, TG and TT

Step 2: Given a root node representing the start sequence "AAAAAA". Step 2.1
- get the neigbhours of the start node and mark them as visited. Step 2.2 -
- get the neighbours of the neigbhours from the previous step and also mark
  them as visited. Step 2.3 - get the neighbours of the neighbours of step 2.2.
  Step 2.4 - apply the brute force algorithm that is comparing every element
  with each other on the list of neighbours from step 2.3 including the root
 node to get a list of nodes/sequences that all differ in at least 3
 positions.

 Step 3: repeat step 2 for all the nodes found in Step 2.4. and also append
 them to the list of already found nodes. continue, until either the number of
 desired sequences has been found or until no new nodes can be found.

 Remarks: The algorithm implemented here is a hybrid between a graph
 theoretical approach and the slow brute force algorithm, The algorithm tries
 to quickly find invalid nodes/sequences and marks them as visited. Using the
 brute force algorithm only on small subsets does not hurt the overall
 performance, The time for building the graph first is negligible w.r.t the
 overall speed compared to the brute force algorithm.

Running the main() generates a graph with gene sequences of length 6 and
then returns 96 sequences that all differ in at least 3 positions/bases.
For demonstration purposes, all intermediate steps are also printed on
the console before returning the actual result. The final result is also
validated using the brute force algorithm.
Example output::
Printing 96 sequences. AAAAAA CCACAA ATAATT AGCACA TTGAAA TAAGAC ACTTAA
AGAAGC GACAGA ACAGTA CGAAAT AATACT GGTAAA AAGGCA TAATCA AATCTA AAATGG
TCAAAG AGAGAG GAGAAT CACAAC CTAACA CAAATG ATCAAG AACTAT GTATAA CATGAA
ACGAAC AAACCC TAAAGT ATACGA AGGCAA TGAATA TACCAA GAACAG TCTCAC CCATCC
CCGCCT CGAAAT CCCTAG CGACGG CTACTC TCACTT CCAGGT GCCCAT TCAAAG GCACGC
CTTCAT CCTCTG GAACAG GTCATC AGAAGC ACAGTA CGAAAT AATACT TCACTT GTTTTT
AGTATG ACCAGT ATTGGT ATCTTA CTAACA CTGGTT CAAATG ATCAAG GAAGTT GTACCT
AGCGTT AGATCT CTACTC TAAAGT TTCACT ATACGA GTAAGG TTATTG TGAATA ATGCTG
ACGTTT TGCAGG TGCCCC AGAAGC CGCGCG AATACT GGGACG AGATCT AGTATG TTCACT
ACCAGT AGTGCC ACCCCG ATCAAG AGCGTT TTTGAG TTGGCC TGGTAC TCGGAT 

Running brute force sanity check. Is this a valid result? Yes!
